Teaching Creedal Proofs to Commoners is Obligatory
Sanusi refutes the denial of teaching creedal proofs to commoners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that teaching creedal proofs to commoners is obligatory and how he refutes the opposing view, including clarifying the intent of al-Ghazālī's statement.

Core Idea
Creedal knowledge requires proof; commoners must be taught proofs to fulfill their duty.

Sanusi tackles a controversial claim: that commoners should not be taught the proofs of Islamic creed. He systematically dismantles this position with multiple arguments, showing that teaching proofs is not only permissible but actually obligatory. The passage also clarifies a famous quote from al-Ghazālī, often misused to support this claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Notice the argumentative structure as Sanusi responds to an objection.
2
Identify the opposing view
Find where Sanusi states the claim he is refuting: that commoners should not be taught creeds or their proofs, without distinction.
3
Trace Sanusi's arguments
List the points Sanusi uses to refute this claim. He uses logical entailments, analogies, and the consensus of scholars.
There are at least six distinct arguments in this passage.
4
Understand the clarification of al-Ghazālī
Sanusi addresses the proof text from al-Ghazālī and explains its true meaning: not to unsettle firm beliefs with doubts, not to withhold teaching.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this issue matters for Islamic education and the responsibility to teach correct doctrine to all Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قول بعض مَنْ لا بصيرة له ولا تحقيق : إِنَّهُ لا تُعلَّمُ العقائد للعوام ، ولا تُذكَرُ لهم براهينها ، مِنْ غير فرق منه بين واضحها الذي يمكنهم فهمُهُ وبينَ غيرِهِ .. فواضحُ الفسادِ ؛ لأنَّهُ إذا كانَتِ المعرفة واجبة على الأعيان بإجماع على ما ذكرَهُ كَثيرٌ مِنَ الأَئِمَّةِ ، بل هي نفسُ الإيمان أو لازمةٌ له ، وهي لا تحصل إلا بالبرهان .. فكيف لا يتأكَّدُ السعي في تعليمهم ما يُحصِّلُها ؟! وإذا جازَتْ قراءة القرآنِ والأحاديث النبوية بحضرتهم مِنْ غيرِ شرح لهم لمعانيهما ، معَ أنَّ فيهما ظواهر يجب تأويلها بإجماع ، وبسببِ فهمها على ظاهرِها هَلَكَ كثيرٌ مِنَ الخَلْقِ .. فَلَأَنْ يجوز تعليمهم العقائد مشروحة بأدلَّتِها التي تسعُها عقولهم أحرى ، بل يتعيَّنُ في حقهم ذلك ؛ لأنَّ التكليف بمعرفة عقائدِ الإيمان بالنظر الصحيح لا فرق فيهِ عند المحققينَ بينَ العامِّي وغيرِهِ ، وإذا كانَ يتعيَّنُ تعليمهم ما يَخصُّهم في الفروع ؛ كالصلاة والزكاة ونحوهما.. فكيف لا يتعيَّن تعليمهم ما يخصهم في أصول دينهم، وما يكونون به مؤمنين حقاً ؟! وزعمُهُ أَنَّهُ لا يُحتاجُ إلى ذلكَ في حقهم ؛ لحصول المعرفة لجميعهم .. مكابرةٌ ، وكذبٌ يفضحُهُ مشاهدة التخليط منه ومنهم في كثيرِ مِنَ العقائدِ ، ولم يحصل لهم الحقُّ فيها ولو بالتقليد ، فكيف بالنظر ؟! وليسَتِ المعرفةُ بالعقائدِ ضروريةً حتى يُدعى حصولها لكلِّ أحدٍ بغير نظر ، بلِ الذي يتبادر إلى الوَهْمِ أوَّلاً إِنَّما هو الفسادُ في كثيرٍ مِنَ العقائدِ حتى يفتحَ الله سبحانه وتعالى لمَنْ شاءَ في تطهير القلبِ مِنْ ذلك بالنظر الصحيح . وأما احتجاجه على ذلكَ بقولِ بعض الأئمة : ( لا تُحرَّكُ على العوام عقائدهم (۱) .. فهَوَس وسوء فهم منه ؛ لأنَّ تحريك عقائدِهم إنَّما يصدقُ في إزالتها مِنْ قلوبهم ، وزحزحتها عن تصميمهم بإيراد شُبَه عليهم تُشكّكهم في الحقِّ ، وتُوجِبُ لهم التردُّد فيه ، كما فعلتِ المبتدعةُ بهم في أزمنة استطالتهم على هذه الأمَّةِ ، وأمَّا تعليم العوام العقائد الصحيحة بأدلَّتِها فليس بتحريك عقائدهم بل هو تقرير لها وإثبات . (۱) هو حجة الإسلام الغزالي ، قال ذلك في الاقتصاد في الاعتقاد » ( ص ١٠٦ ) ، وذاك قوله في حق العامة الذين صح اعتقادهم ، واشتغلوا بعد ذلك إما بعبادة أو صناعة : ( فهؤلاء ينبغي أن يتركوا على ما هم عليه ، ولا تُحرَّكَ عقائدهم بالاستحثاث على تعلم هذا العلم )
As for the saying of someone who has no insight and no verification: that the creeds (al-ʿaqāʾid) should not be taught to the common people (al-ʿawāmm), nor should their proofs be mentioned to them, without him distinguishing between that which is clear and they can understand and that which is not — it is clearly corrupt. Because if knowledge (al-maʿrifa) is individually obligatory by consensus, as many of the imams have mentioned — indeed it is faith itself or necessary for it, and it is only attained through proof (burhān) — then how can striving to teach them what attains it not be emphasized? And if the recitation of the Quran and prophetic hadiths in their presence without explanation of their meanings is permissible, even though they contain apparent meanings (ẓawāhir) that must be interpreted (taʾwīl) by consensus, and due to understanding them in their apparent sense many of creation have perished, then how much more likely that teaching them the creeds explained with their proofs that their minds can accommodate is permissible? Rather, it is incumbent upon them, because the obligation to know the creeds of faith by correct reflection (al-naẓar al-ṣaḥīḥ) is, according to the verifiers, no different between the commoner and others. And if it is incumbent to teach them what pertains to them in the branches (al-furūʿ), like prayer, zakāt, and the like, then how is it not incumbent to teach them what pertains to them in the principles of their religion (uṣūl dīnihim), and that by which they are truly believers? And his claim that this is not needed for them because knowledge is attained for all of them is stubbornness and a lie that is exposed by observing the confusion from him and from them in many of the creeds; and the truth has not been attained by them even by taqlīd, so how about by reflection? And the knowledge of creeds is not necessary (ḍarūriyya) such that it can be claimed that everyone attains it without reflection. Rather, what first comes to mind is corruption in many of the creeds, until God, exalted is He, opens for whom He wills the purification of the heart from that by correct reflection. And as for his argument on that by the saying of some imams: 'Do not stir the creeds of the common people from their place' — it is delusion and misunderstanding. For stirring their creeds is only true in the sense of removing them from their hearts and shifting them from their firmness by presenting to them doubts (shubah) that make them doubt the truth and cause them to hesitate in it, as the innovators (al-mubtadiʿa) did to them in times when they gained ascendancy over this community. As for teaching the common people the correct creeds with their proofs, that is not stirring their creeds but rather confirming them and establishing them. (1) He is the Proof of Islam al-Ghazālī, said that in 'al-Iqtiṣād fī al-Iʿtiqād' (p. 106), and that is his statement concerning the common people whose belief is sound and who after that occupy themselves with either worship or craft: 'These should be left as they are, and their creeds should not be stirred by urging them to learn this science.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of the claim that commoners should not be taught creedal proofs. The author, Sanusi, systematically dismantles this position. He begins by identifying the opposing view: that commoners should not be taught creeds or their proofs, regardless of whether the proofs are clear or abstruse. He declares this view 'clearly corrupt.' He then provides multiple arguments. First, knowledge (maʿrifa) is individually obligatory (wājib ʿaynī) by consensus, and it is attained only through proof (burhān). Therefore, teaching the means to it become obligatory. Second, if it is permissible to recite Quran and hadith to commoners without explanation, even though those texts contain verses that require interpretation and have led many astray when taken literally, then it is even more fitting to teach creeds with explanations and proofs tailored to their intellectual capacity. Third, the obligation to know creed through correct reflection applies equally to the commoner and the elite according to the verifiers (al-muḥaqqiqūn). Fourth, since commoners are taught the branches of religion (furūʿ) like prayer and zakāt, they must likewise be taught the principles (uṣūl) of their religion. Fifth, the claim that commoners already possess knowledge is a lie, as seen in their confusion about many creeds; they have not even attained truth by taqlīd, let alone investigation. Sixth, knowledge of creeds is not innate (ḍarūriyya) — the initial inclination is towards corruption, requiring correct reflection to purify the heart. Finally, he addresses the citation of an imam (al-Ghazālī) who said 'Do not stir the creeds of the common people.' Sanusi explains that this refers to unsettling their firm beliefs by casting doubts, not to teaching them correct creeds with proofs, which actually strengthens their faith.

Key Terms
العقائد
البراهين
العوام
التكليف
النظر الصحيح
التقليد
المعرفة
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that commoners should not be taught any proofs of creed, citing al-Ghazālī's statement 'Do not stir the creeds of the common people.'
Correction: Al-Ghazālī meant not to unsettle their firm beliefs by casting doubts, not to refrain from teaching correct creeds with proofs. Teaching proofs is actually a reinforcement, not a stirring.

Checkpoint
What is Sanusi's main argument for why teaching creedal proofs to commoners is obligatory?
A) Because commoners cannot understand proofs without teaching.
B) Because knowledge of creed is individually obligatory and attained only through proof.
C) Because al-Ghazālī said so.
D) Because commoners are less capable than elites.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi argues that teaching creedal proofs to commoners is not only permissible but obligatory, as it fulfills the duty of knowledge and strengthens faith, contrary to those who misinterpret scholarly warnings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever withheld a creedal proof from someone, assuming they wouldn't understand, thereby failing in your duty to help them attain true faith? What will you change starting today?
?
Are you content to simply follow the beliefs of your family or community without personally reflecting on the proofs of your faith? If so, what is holding you back from seeking that knowledge?
?
When you encounter someone who dismisses the need to teach proofs to 'common people,' do you recognize the harm in that view? How will you respond to such a claim with the clarity of this lesson?

Teaching Common People Correct Beliefs is Obligatory
Sanusi argues for the obligation of teaching common people correct beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation of teaching common people the fundamentals of Islamic creed and why the claim of innate knowledge is false.

Core Idea
Teaching creed is more essential than teaching legal branches.

Sanusi addresses a critical objection: why bother teaching common people complex theological matters? He argues compellingly that if we teach them practical religious duties, we must teach them the foundations of belief. This lesson unpacks his argument and the refutation of the claim that knowledge is innate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the full argument.
Notice the tone of refutation.
2
Identify the a fortiori argument
Identify how Sanusi compares teaching furu' (branches) to teaching usul (foundations). Understand why the latter is more necessary.
This is an argument from stronger to weaker.
3
Examine the refutation of innate knowledge
Sanusi rejects the claim that common people already know the truth. Find his proof from observable reality.
He calls it stubbornness and a lie.
4
Understand the role of reflection (nazar)
Recognize that correct belief requires intellectual effort, not just imitation. Only through proper reflection can the heart be purified.

عند المحققين بين العامي وغيره، وإذا كان يتعين تعليمهم ما يخصهم في الفروع؛ كالصلاة والزكاة ونحوهما.. فكيف لا يتعين تعليمهم ما يخصهم في أصول دينهم، وما يكونون به مؤمنين حقاً؟! وزعمه أنه لا يحتاج إلى ذلك في حقهم؛ لحصول المعرفة لجميعهم .. مكابرة، وكذب يفضحه مشاهدة التخليط منه ومنهم في كثير من العقائد، ولم يحصل لهم الحق فيها ولو بالتقليد، فكيف بالنظر؟! وليست المعرفة بالعقائد ضرورية حتى يدعى حصولها لكل أحد بغير نظر، بل الذي يتبادر إلى الوهم أولاً إنما هو الفساد في كثير من العقائد حتى يفتح الله سبحانه وتعالى لمن شاء في تطهير القلب من ذلك بالنظر الصحيح
According to the investigators, between the common person and others: if it is necessary to teach them what concerns them in the branches (furu'), such as prayer and zakat and the like, then how is it not necessary to teach them what concerns them in the foundations of their religion (usul dinihim), and that by which they are truly believers? And his claim that there is no need for that in their case because knowledge is obtained for all of them is stubbornness and a lie that is exposed by the observation of confusion from him and from them in many of the beliefs, and the truth has not been obtained for them even by blind imitation (taqlid), so how by reflection (nazar)?! And knowledge of beliefs is not necessary (daruriyya) such that it is claimed that it is obtained for everyone without reflection; rather, what first comes to mind is corruption in many of the beliefs, until Allah, glorified and exalted, opens for whomever He wills the purification of the heart from that through correct reflection.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The author begins by establishing a comparison: if it is obligatory to teach common people about practical religious duties (like prayer and zakat), then it is even more obligatory to teach them about the foundations of their religion (usul al-din), because without correct belief, they cannot be true believers. This is an a fortiori argument (qiyas aulawi). The author then refutes the opponent's claim that common people do not need such teaching because they already possess knowledge of these matters innately. He denounces this as stubbornness and a lie, pointing out that observable reality shows confusion among them regarding many beliefs. Even if they had some belief by way of taqlid, it is not sufficient. He then clarifies that knowledge of beliefs is not intuitive (daruri) such that it can be obtained without reflection. On the contrary, what initially occurs to the mind is corruption in many beliefs, and only through correct reflection (nazar) can Allah purify the heart.

Misconception: Common people do not need to learn kalam because they already have innate knowledge of correct beliefs.
Correction: Observable reality shows confusion among common people about many beliefs; true knowledge requires reflection (nazar), not innate intuition.

?
When you see confusion or false beliefs among common Muslims, do you dismiss it as inevitable, or do you feel a personal responsibility to correct it? What step will you take today to ensure those around you have true faith?

Refuting the Misuse of the Saying Not to Stir Beliefs
Sanusi distinguishes between harmful stirring and beneficial teaching of beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct meaning of the prohibition against stirring beliefs and why teaching correct beliefs with proofs is not only permissible but praiseworthy.

Core Idea
Teaching correct beliefs is not stirring; it is confirming and strengthening.

Some argue that we should not disturb common people's beliefs, using a saying from the imams. Sanusi shows this is a misunderstanding. He explains that 'stirring' means casting doubts to uproot correct beliefs. Teaching correct beliefs with proofs does the opposite: it confirms and strengthens faith. He then argues that if beliefs are corrupt, we must stir them out. This passage clarifies a critical methodological principle for Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how Sanusi begins by dismissing the opponent's argument as 'madness and misunderstanding'.
The passage is quite long but forms a single argument.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Sanusi distinguishes two cases: (1) teaching correct beliefs to those who already have correct beliefs, and (2) removing corrupt beliefs. Notice the difference in his ruling for each.
The first case is not stirring; the second case is required.
3
Understand the key distinction
The key is the definition of 'tahrik' (stirring). It is not teaching, but casting doubts to uproot. Teaching strengthens; doubts weaken.
Sanusi uses the Quranic verse to support the removal of falsehood.
4
Reflect on the pedagogical principle
This lesson shows that teaching correct beliefs with proofs is an act of advice and worship. It elevates from taqlid to ma'rifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما احتجاجه على ذلك بقول بعض الأئمة: (لا تحرك على العوام عقائدهم) .. فهو هوس وسوء فهم منه؛ لأن تحريك عقائدهم إنما يصدق في إزالتها من قلوبهم، وزحزحتها عن تصميمهم بإيراد شبه عليهم تشككهم في الحق، وتوجب لهم التردد فيه، كما فعلت بهم في أزمنة استطالتهم على هذه الأمة، وأما تعليم العوام العقائد الصحيحة، ثم تأييدها مع ذلك بالبراهين القطعية المتضح فهمها لديهم؛ بطول التكرار الذي يوجب للنفس الطمأنينة، وعدم قبولها التشكك في الحق بوجه من الوجوه .. فلا يخفى أن هذا من أعظم النصيحة لهم، ومن أفضل ما يتقرب به إلى الله تعالى، وليس فيه تحريك لعقائدهم الصحيحة، بل هو تثبيت لها وتقوية لرسوخها ونقل للمقلد منهم فيها من درجة التقليد المختلف في إيمان صاحبه إلى درجة المعرفة المعتد بها إجماعاً. نعم؛ إذا كانت في قلوبهم عقائد فاسدة فلا شك أن بذكر الحق وإيضاح برهانه يتحرك ذلك الباطل وينزعج للخروج، بل نقذف بالحق على الباطل فيدمغه فإذا هو زاهق [الأنبياء:18]. ولا خفاء: أن التحريك لمثل هذه العقائد المهلكة صاحبها في الآخرة، والسعي في تطهير قلبه منها وإنقاذه من وثاق أسرها .. متعين على كل من له قدرة على ذلك، ويرجى له من ثواب الله تعالى على بمحض فضله جل وعز ما لا يفي بعدده ديوان، ولا يضبطه ميزان، ولأن يهدي الله تعالى بك رجلاً واحداً.. خير لك من حمر
As for his argument by the saying of some imams: 'Do not stir the beliefs of the common people' — it is madness and misunderstanding on his part, because 'stirring their beliefs' only applies to removing them from their hearts and uprooting them from their conviction by introducing doubts that make them doubt the truth and cause them to hesitate in it, as done to them in times of their predominance over this ummah. As for teaching the common people correct beliefs, then supporting them with demonstrative proofs whose understanding is clear to them through long repetition that brings tranquility to the soul and prevents acceptance of doubt about the truth in any way — it is no secret that this is among the greatest advice for them and among the best acts by which one draws near to Allah, and there is no stirring of their correct beliefs; rather it is a confirmation and strengthening of their firmness and a transfer of the imitator among them from the level of imitation (taqlid) regarding which the iman of its possessor is disputed to the level of knowledge (ma'rifa) which is considered valid by consensus. Yes, if there are corrupt beliefs in their hearts, there is no doubt that by mentioning the truth and clarifying its proof, that falsehood is stirred and disturbed to leave. Rather, 'We hurl truth against falsehood, and it destroys it, and behold it vanishes' [21:18]. And it is no secret that stirring such beliefs that destroy their possessor in the Hereafter, and striving to purify his heart from them and save him from the bonds of their captivity, is incumbent upon everyone who has the ability to do so, and he hopes from the reward of Allah Almighty by His pure bounty, glorified and exalted, that which no register can count nor scale measure. 'If Allah guides through you a single man, it is better for you than red...'
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument that one should not disturb the beliefs of common people. The author attacks the opponent's use of the quote from some imams as madness and misunderstanding. He explains that 'stirring beliefs' (tahrik al-'aqa'id) refers specifically to removing beliefs from hearts by casting doubts, thereby causing hesitation. The author contrasts this with teaching correct beliefs and supporting them with definitive proofs. Such teaching is not disturbance; it is confirmation (tathbit) and strengthening (taqwiyat). It elevates the common person from the level of taqlid (whose iman is disputed) to the level of certain knowledge (ma'rifa) that is valid by consensus. Then the author addresses the case of false beliefs: if the common person has corrupt beliefs, then by presenting the truth and clarifying its proof, the falsehood is stirred and expelled. This is praiseworthy and even obligatory. He cites the Quranic verse [21:18] to illustrate that truth destroys falsehood. He concludes by stating that removing such destructive beliefs is incumbent on those who have the ability, and the reward for guiding even one person is immense, alluding to the hadith about red camels.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That teaching a common person new beliefs after they already have beliefs is disturbing their faith.
Correction: Sanusi explains that teaching correct beliefs with proofs is not disturbing but confirming; disturbing only occurs when doubts are cast to uproot already correct beliefs.

Checkpoint
What does the author say is the true meaning of 'stirring the beliefs of common people'?
A) Teaching them correct beliefs
B) Casting doubts to uproot their correct beliefs
C) Making them reflect on their beliefs
D) Changing their beliefs to match the scholar's view

Key Takeaway
Teaching correct beliefs with proofs strengthens faith, while stirring applies only to casting doubts to remove correct beliefs; removing corrupt beliefs is obligatory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Teaching Proofs to the Common People: A Defense
Sanusi defends teaching proofs to common people as strengthening faith, not harming it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that teaching definitive proofs to common people strengthens their faith, moves them from imitation to certainty, and is a great act of counsel—not a cause of harm.

Core Idea
Teaching common people definitive proofs does not weaken faith—it moves them from imitation to certainty.

Sanusi addresses a common concern: that teaching theological proofs to ordinary believers might disturb their simple faith. In this passage, he argues the opposite—that such teaching, done with repetition and clarity, actually strengthens faith, removes doubts, and even helps those with false beliefs return to the truth. He considers this one of the greatest forms of sincere counsel to the community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the full argument.
Notice the passionate tone and the use of Quranic verse and hadith.
2
Identify Sanusi's main claim
Find where Sanusi states that teaching proofs to common people benefits both those with correct beliefs and those with false beliefs.
He says it does not disturb correct beliefs but strengthens them.
3
Examine the treatment of false beliefs
See how he uses the Quranic verse (Al-Anbiya' 18) to argue that truth crushes falsehood when presented with proof.
He considers stirring false beliefs a necessary step for purification.
4
Reflect on the lament and conclusion
Consider Sanusi's criticism of scholars who neglect usul al-din and his call to gratitude for those who attain the truth.
This shows the urgency of the issue in his time.

العقائد الصحيحة ، ثم تأييدها مع ذلكَ بالبراهين القطعية المتَّضِحِ فهمها لديهم ؛ بطولِ التكرار الذي يُوجِبُ للنفسِ الطُّمأنينةَ ، وعدم قبولِها التشكُكَ في الحقِّ بوجهِ مِنَ الوجوه .. فلا يخفى أنَّ هذا مِنْ أعظم النصيحة لهم ، ومِنْ أفضل ما يُتقرَّبُ بِهِ إِلى اللهِ تعالى ، وليس فيه تحريك لعقائدهم الصحيحة ، بل هو تثبيت لها وتقوية لرسوخها ونقل للمُقدِّدِ منهم فيها مِنْ درجةِ التقليدِ المُختلفِ في إيمانِ صاحبِهِ إلى درجة المعرفة المعتد بها إجماعاً
نعم ؛ إذا كانَتْ في قلوبهم عقائد فاسدة فلا شكَ أَنَّ بذكرِ الحقِّ وإيضاح برهانِهِ يتحرَّكُ ذلكَ الباطل وينزعج للخروج ، بَلْ نَقْذِفُ بِالْحَقِّ عَلَى الْبَاطِلِ فَيَدْمَعُهُ فَإِذَا هُوَ زَاهِقٌ [الأنبياء : ۱۸]
ولا خفاءَ : أنَّ التحريكَ لمثل هذهِ العقائدِ المهلكة صاحبَها في الآخرة ، والسعي في تطهير قلبهِ منها وإنقاذِهِ مِنْ وَثَاقِ أَسرِها . . مُتعيِّن على كلِّ مَنْ له قدرة على ذلكَ ، ويُرجى لهُ مِنْ ثواب الله تعالى على بمحض فضلِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ ما لا يفي بعَدِّهِ ديوان ، ولا يضبطه ميزان ، وَلَأَنْ يَهْدِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِكَ رَجُلاً وَاحِداً خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنْ حُمْرِ النَّعَمِ أي : مِنَ التصدق بها
وبالجملة : فتقرير عقائدِ التوحيدِ ببراهينها الواضحة على العوام لا يزيدهم إلا خيراً ؛ لأنَّ الضالّ منهم يرجعُ عن ضلاله ، والمهتدي يزدادُ هُدى وقوَّةً في إيمانِهِ ، ورسوخاً في إيقانِهِ ؛ فالسعي في قطع ذلك شَيْطَةٌ لا شك فيها
وما أحوج كثيراً مِنْ مُتفقهة زماننا إلى تعلمهم أصول دينهم ، والاشتغال بما يعنيهم عن كثير مما لا يعنيهم ! فكيف بعوامهم ؟! لكن أينَ الحقُّ ؟! وأينَ أهلُهُ ؟! وأينَ مَنْ يقبلُه على تقدير وجودِهِ نادراً ؟! فمَنْ ظفر بمعرفةِ الحقِّ في هذا الزمانِ ، ثم وُفِّقَ للعمل به .. فليكثر مِنْ شكر الله تعالى غاية جهدِهِ ، وليَعُدَّ ذلكَ مِنْ خوارق العادةِ في هذا الزمانِ ، والله المستعانُ ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله .
The correct beliefs, then supporting them with definitive proofs whose understanding is clear to them; by the length of repetition that causes the soul tranquility, and the non-acceptance of doubting the truth in any way... So it is not hidden that this is among the greatest counsel for them, and among the best acts by which one draws near to Allah Almighty, and it does not involve disturbing their correct beliefs, but rather it is a confirmation for them and a strengthening of their rootedness, and a transfer for the one who is a muqallid among them from the degree of taqlid (blind imitation) regarding which there is disagreement about the faith of its possessor, to the degree of ma'rifa (certain knowledge) that is relied upon by consensus. Yes; if there are corrupt beliefs in their hearts, there is no doubt that by mentioning the truth and clarifying its proof, that falsehood is stirred and distressed to exit; rather, 'We hurl the truth against falsehood, and it crushes it, and lo, it vanishes' [Al-Anbiya' 18]. And it is not hidden: that stirring such beliefs that destroy their possessor in the Hereafter, and striving to purify his heart from them and rescue him from the bond of their captivity... is incumbent upon everyone who has the ability to do so, and is hoped for him from the reward of Allah Almighty—by His pure grace, may He be exalted and glorified—what a register cannot count, nor a scale measure; 'For Allah to guide through you a single man is better for you than red camels' i.e., than giving them in charity. In summary: presenting the beliefs of tawhid (monotheism) with their clear proofs to the common people does not increase them except in goodness; because the misguided among them returns from his misguidance, and the rightly guided increases in guidance and strength in his faith, and rootedness in his certainty. So striving to cut that off is a devilish prompting, no doubt about it. And how much in need are many of the mutafaqqiha (students of fiqh) of our time to learn the principles of their religion, and to occupy themselves with what concerns them, instead of much that does not concern them! So how about their common people?! But where is the truth?! And where are its people?! And where is one who accepts it, given its rarity?! So whoever obtains knowledge of the truth in this time, and then is granted success to act upon it... let him thank Allah Almighty as much as he can, and consider that among the extraordinary things in this time. And Allah is the one sought for help, and there is no power and no strength except through Allah.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a defense of teaching theological proofs to the common people ('awamm). The author argues that such teaching, when done with definitive proofs and repeated explanation, does not disturb correct beliefs but rather strengthens them and moves the believer from mere taqlid (imitation) to certain knowledge (ma'rifa). If the person already holds false beliefs, hearing the truth and its evidence will upset and expel that falsehood, as the Quranic verse states: 'We hurl the truth against falsehood, and it crushes it.' The author then emphasizes that removing corrupt beliefs is a religious duty for those able, with immense reward. He concludes that teaching tawhid to 'awamm always benefits: the misguided return and the guided grow stronger. He laments that even scholars of fiqh neglect usul al-din, and encourages gratitude for those few who attain the truth.

Refuting Taqlid in the Principles of Religion
Sanusi refutes taqlid in usul al-din and praises the science of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the science of kalam is superior to blind imitation in the principles of religion and why taqlid is condemned.

Core Idea
Blind imitation in creed is lowly and harmful; Allah guides those He loves to reasoned faith.

Sanusi opens his discussion of methodology by making a bold claim: the science of kalam is the most excellent and most obligatory of sciences. But he also warns against mere imitation in matters of belief. This passage sets the stage for the entire study of theology by distinguishing between the path of guidance and the path of ruin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the strong language used for taqlid.
2
Identify the two groups described
The passage contrasts those whom Allah intends good for with those satisfied with taqlid. List their respective outcomes.
3
Reflect on the term 'taqlid'
Understand what taqlid means in this context: accepting beliefs without proof.
This is a key term.
4
Connect to your own learning
Ask yourself: why is it important to seek proof for beliefs, rather than just follow what others say?
This lesson establishes the rationale for studying kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال القول بالتقليد في أصول الدين
وبالجملة: فمَنْ أَرادَ اللهُ بهِ خيراً عرَّفَهُ مراشده ، وفتح له في معرفةِ هذا العلم الذي هو أفضلُ العلوم وأوجبها ، وأولى ما يشتغل به كلُّ مُوفَّقِ ، والرضا بحرفةِ التقليدِ دناءة في الهمَّةِ والدين ، وتعرُّض لما يُخشى مِنْ عظم عذابِ القبرِ ، وهولِ الخلودِ في النار والعياذ بالله
Refuting the claim of taqlid (blind imitation) in the principles of religion. In summary: Whoever Allah intends good for, He makes known to him his proper paths, and opens for him understanding of this science ('ilm) which is the most excellent and most obligatory of sciences, and the most worthy pursuit for every divinely aided person. And being satisfied with the craft of taqlid is baseness in aspiration and religion, and exposure to what is feared of the great punishment of the grave, and the terror of eternity in the Fire—and we seek refuge with Allah.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a succinct refutation of taqlid in usul al-din (the principles of religion). The author states that the one Allah intends good for is guided to understand 'this science'—meaning the science of kalam ('ilm al-kalam)—which is described as the best and most obligatory of sciences, and the most deserving of attention for every successful person. In contrast, being content with taqlid is considered lowliness in both aspiration and religion, and it exposes one to severe punishment in the grave and the terror of eternal punishment in Hell. The passage thus establishes the superiority of reasoned faith (based on proof) over blind imitation in the most fundamental matters of belief.

Key Terms

أصول الدين
هذا العلم
المراشد
دناءة
عذاب القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think taqlid is acceptable in all religious matters.
Correction: The author restricts its condemnation to the principles of religion (usul al-din) and praises the science of kalam as the proper method.

Checkpoint
How does the author describe the person who is satisfied with taqlid in the principles of religion?
A) As being divinely aided and blessed.
B) As having low aspiration and religion, and exposed to punishment.
C) As being excused because of their inability.
D) As following the way of the righteous predecessors.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi teaches that the science of kalam is the most excellent science, and that blind imitation in creed is an act of spiritual baseness that incurs divine punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief about Allah or the afterlife simply because you were raised with it, without seeking to understand the proof? If so, are you not exposed to the punishment this passage warns of? What will you do today to start seeking that understanding?
?
Do you truly desire Allah to intend good for you? If yes, then where is your effort to learn the science of kalam or at least the proofs of your creed? Leave aside the comfort of imitation and ask yourself: are you satisfied with baseness in your religion?
?
The terror of eternity in the Fire is a real possibility for those who persist in taqlid in creed. What specific belief do you hold that you cannot prove from reason or revelation? What is stopping you from verifying it? Commit today to learning the evidence for one foundational belief.

Teaching Aqeedah with Proofs
Sanusi argues for teaching proofs of tawhid to commoners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi’s argument for teaching theological proofs to common people and why he considers preventing it a devilish act.

Core Idea
Teaching aqeedah with proofs benefits everyone: the misguided return and the guided strengthen.

Sanusi makes a passionate case for teaching the clear proofs of tawhid to laypeople. He argues that such teaching only brings good: it guides the misguided and strengthens the faithful. He then laments those who neglect this duty, calling opposition to it satanic. This passage reveals the practical concern of a theologian for the spiritual welfare of the community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp Sanusi's flow.
Notice the strong opening statement 'لا يزيدهم إلا خيراً'.
2
Identify the two benefits
Sanusi explains that teaching proofs helps the misguided return and the guided increase in faith and certainty. Highlight these in the text.
3
Reflect on his lament
Read his criticism of 'pseudo-jurists' and his remarks about the scarcity of truth. Consider why he calls opposition 'devilish'.
He concludes that attaining truth in that time is a miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة : فتقرير عقائدِ التوحيدِ ببراهينها الواضحة على العوام لا يزيدهم إلا خيراً ؛ لأنَّ الضالّ منهم يرجعُ عن ضلاله ، والمهتدي يزدادُ هُدى وقوَّةً في إيمانِهِ ، ورسوخاً في إيقانِهِ ؛ فالسعي في قطع ذلك شَيطة لا شك فيها . وما أحوج كثيراً مِنْ مُتفقهة زماننا إلى تعلمهم أصول دينهم ، والاشتغال بما يعنيهم عن كثير مما لا يعنيهم ! فكيف بعوامهم ؟! لكن أينَ الحقُّ ؟! وأينَ أهلُهُ ؟! وأينَ مَنْ يقبلُه على تقدير وجودِهِ نادراً ؟! فمَنْ ظفر بمعرفةِ الحقِّ في هذا الزمانِ ، ثم وُفِّقَ للعمل به .. فليكثر مِنْ شكر الله تعالى غاية جهدِهِ ، وليَعُدَّ ذلكَ مِنْ خوارق العادةِ في هذا الزمانِ ، والله المستعانُ ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله .
In summary: presenting the doctrines of tawhid (monotheism) with their clear proofs to the common people does not increase them except in goodness; because the misguided among them returns from his misguidance, and the guided increases in guidance and strength in his faith, and firmness in his certainty. So striving to cut that off is an undeniable devilish act. How much more do many of the pseudo-jurists of our time need to learn the fundamentals of their religion and occupy themselves with what concerns them over much that does not concern them! How about their common people?! But where is the truth?! And where are its people?! And where is the one who accepts it, if it exists, rarely?! So whoever attains knowledge of the truth in this time, and then is granted success to act upon it, let him abundantly thank Allah Almighty with all his effort, and consider that as one of the miracles (khawariq al-‘ada) in this time. And Allah is the Grantor of success, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah.

Commentary
This passage is an argument in favor of teaching Aqeedah with proofs to the common people. The author begins by stating his thesis: presenting the clear proofs of tawhid to laypeople only increases them in good. He then explains why: the misguided person abandons his error, and the guided person gains more strength in faith and certainty. Therefore, any attempt to prevent such teaching is undoubtedly a satanic act. He then laments the state of many jurists of his time who neglect learning usul al-din while busying themselves with what is less important, so how much more so for the common people? He expresses regret over the scarcity of truth and those who accept it. He concludes by encouraging anyone who attains knowledge of the truth and acts upon it to thank Allah abundantly, considering it a miracle in that age, and ends with a prayer for divine assistance.

Nullifying Taqleed in the Fundamentals of Religion
Sanusi refutes taqleed as insufficient for knowledge in usul al-din.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why taqleed (blind imitation) cannot produce the certainty required for true faith, and how Sanusi uses hadith and logical reasoning to refute it.

Core Idea
Faith requires certainty, but taqleed can only give contradictory assents — not true knowledge.

Sanusi begins by declaring that taqleed has no place in the fundamentals of religion. He argues that faith demands certainty and knowledge, which can only be attained through sound reflection, not blind imitation. To prove this, he cites two hadiths that make certainty a condition for entry into Paradise, and then presents a logical demonstration that taqleed-based assent cannot be considered knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the English translation to understand the overall meaning before analysis.
Notice the strong language: 'dana'a' (baseness) and 'ta'arud' (exposure).
2
Identify the two main pieces of evidence
Sanusi uses two hadiths to show that certainty is required. Find them and note what they say about the condition for Paradise.
The hadiths are from Abu Hurairah and Muslim.
3
Understand the logical argument
Sanusi argues that if taqleed-based assent were knowledge, contradictory assents could both be true. Why is that impossible? Because knowledge is an attribute that does not admit opposites.
Think about how this shows taqleed cannot produce genuine certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال القول بالتقليد في أصول الدين ] وبالجملة : فمَنْ أَرادَ اللهُ بهِ خيراً عرَّفَهُ مراشده ، وفتح له في معرفةِ هذا العلم الذي هو أفضلُ العلوم وأوجبها ، وأولى ما يشتغل به كلُّ مُوفَّقِ ، والرضا بحرفةِ التقليدِ دناءة في الهمَّةِ والدين ، وتعرُّض لما يُخشى مِنْ عظم عذابِ القبرِ ، وهولِ الخلودِ في النار والعياذ بالله تعالى (۱) ؛ لأنَّ المطلوب في الإيمانِ اليقين والمعرفة ، وذلك لا يكونُ إلا بالنظر الصحيح . وفي حديث أبي هريرةَ رضي الله تعالى عنه : ( مَنْ لَقِيتَ وَرَاءَ هَذَا الْحَائِطِ يَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إلا اللهُ مُسْتَيْقِناً قَلْبُهُ . . فَبَشِّرْهُ بِالْجَنَّةِ (٢) وفي ( مسلم ) : ( مَنْ مَاتَ وَهُوَ يَعْلَمُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إلا الله . . دَخَلَ الْجَنَّةَ ((٣) فانظر كيف شرط في هذين الحديثين اليقين والعلم ، وهما ضدَّانِ ولا يصح أنْ يُقالَ : ( الجزم لأجل التقليد علم ) لأنَّهُ لو كانَ ذلكَ الجزمُ علماً .. لزم اجتماع الضدين (٥) ؛ في الجزم بحدوثه تقليداً ، والجزم بقدمِهِ كذلكَ أيضاً ؛ لأنَّ العلم صفةٌ لا تحتمل النقيض بوجه ، فيلزمُ أنْ يكونَ العالم في نفس الأمر قديماً وحادثاً ! وذلكَ ممَّا لا يُعقَلُ . وهذان الحديثانِ يُفسّرانَ كلَّ ما أُجمِلَ مِنْ أحاديث الشهادتين
[Chapter: Nullifying the claim of taqleed (blind imitation) in the fundamentals of religion] In summary: whoever Allah intends good for, He makes him know his ways, and opens for him knowledge of this science, which is the best of sciences and the most obligatory, and the most deserving of occupation for every successful person. And being content with the profession of taqleed is baseness in aspiration and religion, and an exposure to what is feared of the great punishment of the grave and the terror of eternal fire – may Allah protect us – because what is required in faith is certainty and knowledge, and that is only attained through sound reflection (nazar saheeh). And in the hadith of Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Whoever you meet behind this wall, testifying that there is no deity but Allah, with his heart certain, then give him glad tidings of Paradise.' And in Sahih Muslim: 'Whoever dies while he knows that there is no deity but Allah enters Paradise.' So see how in these two hadiths, certainty ('ilm) and knowledge (yaqeen) are conditions, and they are opposites [to ignorance?]. And it is not valid to say: 'Assent (jazzm) for the sake of taqleed is knowledge' because if that assent were knowledge, then the coexistence of opposites would be necessary: in the assent of its occurrence through taqleed, and the assent of its pre-eternity likewise also, because knowledge is an attribute that does not admit of contradiction in any way. So it would necessitate that the person who knows is, in the same respect, both pre-eternal and temporal! And that is unintelligible. And these two hadiths explain all that is summarized from the hadiths of the two testimonies.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of taqleed (blind imitation) in the fundamentals of religion. It begins with a section heading declaring the nullification of the claim of taqleed in usul al-din. The author states that whoever Allah intends good for, He opens for him the knowledge of this science (the science of kalam), which is the best and most obligatory of sciences. Then he criticizes being content with taqleed as a low aspiration and a danger to one's religion. The reason is that faith requires certainty and knowledge, which can only be attained through sound reflection (nazar saheeh). To support this, he cites two hadiths: one from Abu Hurairah requiring certainty in the heart, and one from Muslim requiring knowledge. He then makes a logical argument: if one claims that assent (jazzm) due to taqleed is knowledge, then two contradictory assents could both be considered knowledge: for example, one person assents with certainty that the world is originated based on taqleed, and another assents with certainty that it is pre-eternal based on taqleed. Since knowledge cannot admit contradiction, this would require the person who knows to be both knowledgeable of its origination and its pre-eternity, which is impossible. Therefore, taqleed cannot be considered knowledge. Finally, he notes that these two hadiths explain all that has been summarized from the hadiths about the two testimonies (shahadatayn).

اليقين
العلم
النظر الصحيح
الجزم
الضدين

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One may think that assenting to the truth based on the authority of scholars is sufficient for knowledge.
Correction: Sanusi shows that taqleed cannot produce the certainty required for true faith because it would allow contradictory certainties, which is impossible for knowledge.

Checkpoint

A) Because taqleed is forbidden in all matters.
B) Because it would allow contradictory certainties to coexist, which is impossible for knowledge.
C) Because the hadiths only require saying the shahada, not certainty.
D) Because taqleed is only for common people, not scholars.

Key Takeaway
Taqleed cannot generate the certainty required for true faith; only sound reflection (nazar) leads to genuine knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If your belief in Allah depends on the authority of a scholar or your parents rather than on your own certainty, would you be willing to stand before Him with that excuse?
?
The hadith requires certainty of heart for Paradise. Look at your own heart: is there any doubt, any area where you rely on 'taqleed' rather than personal conviction? How will you seek certainty starting today?

The Hadith of Jibril: The Objection and Its Refutation
Sanusi presents and refutes the objection from the Hadith of Jibril.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the flawed logic behind using the Hadith of Jibril to justify taqlid, and the correct interpretation that iman requires rational knowledge.

Core Idea
Iman requires knowledge, and knowledge requires nazar—taqlid falls short.

Sanusi begins by presenting a common but mistaken argument: some people claim that the famous hadith of Jibril shows that accepting beliefs by taqlid is sufficient for iman. They reason that since the Prophet simply listed the pillars without mentioning proofs, rational inquiry (nazar) cannot be a condition. However, Sanusi immediately declares this interpretation false and explains the proper understanding of the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first part where Sanusi presents the argument of those who rely on taqlid. Notice how they use the Prophet's silence on proofs as evidence.
The objection hinges on the assumption that if nazar were necessary, the Prophet would have mentioned proofs.
2
Understand the refutation
Sanusi states that this understanding is absolutely false. He then explains the meaning of the Prophet's words according to Ash'ari and others, showing that iman is knowledge or based on knowledge, which requires correct nazar.
3
Connect to the core idea
Reflect on why the necessity of nazar is derived from the same hadith. This shows that the objection fails because it misinterprets the Prophet's intent.
Iman and knowledge are intrinsically linked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وممَّا يَركنُ إليه في الاكتفاء بالتقليدِ بعضُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : الحديث الصحيحُ المشهورُ ؛ وهو حديث عبدِ اللهِ بنِ عمرَ عن رضي الله عنهما في سؤالِ جبريل عليه السلام النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلّمَ عنِ الإيمان والإسلام والإحسان (۱) ، في تفسيرِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لها بما هو معروف مشهورٌ ، فيقولُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : دلَّ الحديث على أنَّ مَنْ حفظَ تلك الخصال المفسَّرَ بها الإيمان وفهمها واعتقدها ولو بالتقليد .. فهو مؤمن ؛ إذ لو كانَ حصولها بالنظر شرطاً في كونها إيماناً لَمَا اقتصر النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في تفسيرِ الإِيمَانِ على عدها دونَ ذكرِ أدلَّتِها . (( أن وهذا الأخذُ مِنَ الحديثِ باطل قطعاً ؛ لأنَّ قولَه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في شرح الإيمانِ : « أَنْ تُؤْمِنَ بِاللهِ . . . (۲) إلى آخرِهِ : معناه عند الشيخ الأشعري : أن تعرف ذلك ، وعند القاضي وغيرِهِ تُحدِّثَ نفْسَكَ بذلك حديثاً تابعاً للمعرفة(۳) ، وعلى كلا القولين فالمعرفة التي هي نفس الإيمان أو لازمةٌ له.. لا تحصل إلا بالنظر الصحيح ، وذلك يستلزم أنَّ الإيمان على القولين لا يحصل إلا بالنظر الصحيح وإنما لم يبين لهم النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أدلتها ؛ لأنَّها عقليَّةٌ ، لا تتوقَّفُ على بيان الشارع لها ، ولاكتفائه أيضاً بما في القرآنِ مِنَ الأدلَّةِ الكثيرة عليها ، وإنَّما بيَّنَ لهم صلّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ما لا يُعرَفُ إلا مِنَ الشرع ؛ وهو أنَّ معرفة هذه الخصالِ هي الإيمانُ الشرعي الذي يترتب عليه الدخول في الجنَّةِ وإن لم يوفِ بفروع الشريعةِ ، حتى يُؤخَذُ مِنْ تفسيره الإيمان بطلان مذهب المعتزلة في جعلهم الأعمال الواجبة جزءاً منه ، وأنَّ مَنْ لم يوفِ بها فليس بمؤمن ، ويُؤخَذُ منه أيضاً تكفيرهم ؛ لنقصهم خصلةٌ مِنْ خصال الإيمانِ ؛ وهي معرفةُ القَدَرِ ومن فوائدِ تفسيره صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّم للإيمان : أنَّ المكلف إذا عرف حقيقته بحث عن تحصيل هذه الحقيقة ومعرفتها بالنظر الصحيح ، أما إذا لم يعرف حقيقةَ الإيمانِ فقد يُحصِّلُ معرفة أشياءَ مِنَ الأجنبية عنه ؛ كعلم النجومِ والطب ونحوهما ، أو يحصل معرفة بعض خصالِ الإيمانِ فقط ، ويتوهَّمُ لجهلِهِ بحقيقةِ الإِيمَانِ أَنَّهُ قد حصل حقيقته ، وأنَّهُ مؤمن شرعاً ، وهو ليس كذلك ، وقس على هذه الفوائد ما يليقُ بكلام مَنْ أُوتِيَ جوامعَ الكَلِمِ وأمَّا فهُمُ صحَةِ التقليدِ مِنْ هذا الحديثِ فلا يخفى أَنَّهُ فهم ركيك في غاية ، ويدلُّكَ على غاية ركاكتِهِ زيادةً على ما سبق : أنَّ التقليد في هذه الخصال التي فُسِّرَ بها الإيمانُ باعتبار ثبوتِ مدلولها وصحته.
And among what some who have no insight rely upon for sufficiency with taqlid is the well-known authentic hadith; it is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, in the question of Jibril, peace be upon him, to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, about iman, Islam, and ihsan (1), in his interpretation, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, of them by what is well known and famous. So one who has no insight says: The hadith indicates that whoever memorizes those characteristics by which iman is interpreted, understands them, and believes them, even if by taqlid, then he is a believer; for if their attainment through nazar were a condition for their being iman, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would not have confined himself in interpreting iman to enumerating them without mentioning their proofs. (This) and this taking from the hadith is absolutely false; because his statement, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in explaining iman: 'That you believe in Allah... (2) to its end,' its meaning according to al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that you know that, and according to al-Qadi and others is that you speak to yourself with that speech following knowledge (3), and on both sayings, knowledge which is itself iman or necessary for it is not obtained except by correct nazar. And that necessitates that iman on both sayings is not obtained except by correct nazar. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, only did not explain their proofs to them because they are rational, not dependent on the Lawgiver's explanation for them, and also because of his sufficiency with what is in the Quran of abundant proofs for them. Rather, he, peace be upon him, explained to them what is not known except from divine law: that knowledge of these characteristics is the legal iman by which entry into Paradise follows even if one does not fulfill the branches of the Law, so that from his interpretation of iman is taken the invalidity of the Mu'tazilite doctrine in making obligatory acts part of it, and that whoever does not fulfill them is not a believer, and also from it is taken their excommunication for their deficiency of one characteristic of the characteristics of iman, which is knowledge of predestination. And among the benefits of his interpretation, peace be upon him, of iman is that the morally responsible person, if he knows its reality, seeks to acquire this reality and know it by correct nazar. But if he does not know the reality of iman, he may acquire knowledge of things extraneous to it, such as the science of stars and medicine and the like, or he may acquire knowledge of some characteristics of iman only, and he deludes, due to his ignorance of the reality of iman, that he has attained its reality and that he is a believer legally, while he is not so. And analogize to these benefits what befits the speech of one who has been given the comprehensive expressions. As for their understanding the validity of taqlid from this hadith, it is not hidden that it is an extremely weak understanding, and what indicates to you the extreme weakness of it, in addition to what preceded, is that taqlid regarding these characteristics by which iman is interpreted is with respect to the establishment of their implications and their correctness.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of an objection. It begins by stating the objection: some people of little insight rely on the famous hadith of Jibril to argue that taqlid (uncritical acceptance) in matters of faith is sufficient. They argue that if nazar (rational inquiry) were necessary, the Prophet would have mentioned proofs when he explained iman. The author then refutes this objection (wa hadha al-akhdhu min al-hadithi batilun qat'an) by explaining the Prophet's silence on proofs: the proofs are rational (aqliyya), not dependent on revelation, and the Qur'an already contains abundant proofs. The Prophet only explained what is known exclusively from revelation—that these characteristics constitute saving faith. The author then draws several benefits: (1) refuting the Mu'tazila who make works part of iman, (2) excommunicating those who deny predestination, and (3) encouraging the seeker to pursue proper nazar. Finally, he stresses that the very idea of using the hadith to justify taqlid is extremely weak, since taqlid is about the truth of the propositions, not about their acceptance without understanding.

Key Terms
تقليد
نظر
إيمان
معرفة
حديث جبريل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hadith of Jibril shows that accepting beliefs by taqlid without rational inquiry is sufficient for iman.
Correction: The hadith actually defines iman as knowledge, which requires correct nazar; the Prophet's silence on proofs is because they are rational, not because nazar is unnecessary.

C) That you follow tradition
D) That you recite the shahada

Key Takeaway
The Hadith of Jibril does not support taqlid; it actually proves that iman requires knowledge obtained through rational inquiry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been content with just memorizing Islamic beliefs without truly understanding their proofs? How has that affected the strength of your iman? Will you commit to seeking knowledge through nazar from now on?
?
When someone challenges your faith, do you feel confident that you can provide rational proofs, or do you rely on saying 'this is what I was taught'? How can you ensure your belief is grounded in knowledge, not just tradition?
?
If knowledge (ma'rifa) is necessary for iman, what concrete steps will you take today to move from taqlid to certainty? What is one belief you can start investigating rationally this week?

The Prophet's Wisdom and the Benefits of Understanding Iman Correctly
Sanusi explains the wisdom behind the Prophet's omission of proofs and lists the benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet did not mention the proofs of iman, and the important theological benefits derived from his explanation.

Core Idea
The Prophet revealed what only revelation can tell us: the content of saving faith.

Having refuted the objection, Sanusi now explains why the Prophet omitted the proofs: they are rational, not dependent on revelation, and are already abundantly present in the Quran. The Prophet's role was to define what constitutes legal iman, not to provide the arguments for it. This yields several crucial benefits, including the refutation of the Mu'tazila and the importance of seeking correct nazar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reason for silence
Read the part where Sanusi explains that the proofs are rational and already in the Quran. This shows why the Prophet did not need to mention them.
Rational proofs do not depend on the Lawgiver's explanation.
2
Learn the benefits of interpretation
Note the three benefits: refutation of Mu'tazila, excommunication of those who deny predestination, and encouragement to seek nazar.
These benefits show the depth of the Prophetic teaching.
3
Understand the weakness of taqlid
Sanusi concludes that understanding taqlid from the hadith is extremely weak, especially since taqlid concerns the truth of propositions, not mere acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وممَّا يَركنُ إليه في الاكتفاء بالتقليدِ بعضُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : الحديث الصحيحُ المشهورُ ؛ وهو حديث عبدِ اللهِ بنِ عمرَ عن رضي الله عنهما في سؤالِ جبريل عليه السلام النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلّمَ عنِ الإيمان والإسلام والإحسان (۱) ، في تفسيرِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لها بما هو معروف مشهورٌ ، فيقولُ مَنْ لا بصيرة لهُ : دلَّ الحديث على أنَّ مَنْ حفظَ تلك الخصال المفسَّرَ بها الإيمان وفهمها واعتقدها ولو بالتقليد .. فهو مؤمن ؛ إذ لو كانَ حصولها بالنظر شرطاً في كونها إيماناً لَمَا اقتصر النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في تفسيرِ الإِيمَانِ على عدها دونَ ذكرِ أدلَّتِها . (( أن وهذا الأخذُ مِنَ الحديثِ باطل قطعاً ؛ لأنَّ قولَه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في شرح الإيمانِ : « أَنْ تُؤْمِنَ بِاللهِ . . . (۲) إلى آخرِهِ : معناه عند الشيخ الأشعري : أن تعرف ذلك ، وعند القاضي وغيرِهِ تُحدِّثَ نفْسَكَ بذلك حديثاً تابعاً للمعرفة(۳) ، وعلى كلا القولين فالمعرفة التي هي نفس الإيمان أو لازمةٌ له.. لا تحصل إلا بالنظر الصحيح ، وذلك يستلزم أنَّ الإيمان على القولين لا يحصل إلا بالنظر الصحيح وإنما لم يبين لهم النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أدلتها ؛ لأنَّها عقليَّةٌ ، لا تتوقَّفُ على بيان الشارع لها ، ولاكتفائه أيضاً بما في القرآنِ مِنَ الأدلَّةِ الكثيرة عليها ، وإنَّما بيَّنَ لهم صلّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ما لا يُعرَفُ إلا مِنَ الشرع ؛ وهو أنَّ معرفة هذه الخصالِ هي الإيمانُ الشرعي الذي يترتب عليه الدخول في الجنَّةِ وإن لم يوفِ بفروع الشريعةِ ، حتى يُؤخَذُ مِنْ تفسيره الإيمان بطلان مذهب المعتزلة في جعلهم الأعمال الواجبة جزءاً منه ، وأنَّ مَنْ لم يوفِ بها فليس بمؤمن ، ويُؤخَذُ منه أيضاً تكفيرهم ؛ لنقصهم خصلةٌ مِنْ خصال الإيمانِ ؛ وهي معرفةُ القَدَرِ ومن فوائدِ تفسيره صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّم للإيمان : أنَّ المكلف إذا عرف حقيقته بحث عن تحصيل هذه الحقيقة ومعرفتها بالنظر الصحيح ، أما إذا لم يعرف حقيقةَ الإيمانِ فقد يُحصِّلُ معرفة أشياءَ مِنَ الأجنبية عنه ؛ كعلم النجومِ والطب ونحوهما ، أو يحصل معرفة بعض خصالِ الإيمانِ فقط ، ويتوهَّمُ لجهلِهِ بحقيقةِ الإِيمَانِ أَنَّهُ قد حصل حقيقته ، وأنَّهُ مؤمن شرعاً ، وهو ليس كذلك ، وقس على هذه الفوائد ما يليقُ بكلام مَنْ أُوتِيَ جوامعَ الكَلِمِ وأمَّا فهُمُ صحَةِ التقليدِ مِنْ هذا الحديثِ فلا يخفى أَنَّهُ فهم ركيك في غاية ، ويدلُّكَ على غاية ركاكتِهِ زيادةً على ما سبق : أنَّ التقليد في هذه الخصال التي فُسِّرَ بها الإيمانُ باعتبار ثبوتِ مدلولها وصحته.
And among what some who have no insight rely upon for sufficiency with taqlid is the well-known authentic hadith; it is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, in the question of Jibril, peace be upon him, to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, about iman, Islam, and ihsan (1), in his interpretation, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, of them by what is well known and famous. So one who has no insight says: The hadith indicates that whoever memorizes those characteristics by which iman is interpreted, understands them, and believes them, even if by taqlid, then he is a believer; for if their attainment through nazar were a condition for their being iman, the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, would not have confined himself in interpreting iman to enumerating them without mentioning their proofs. (This) and this taking from the hadith is absolutely false; because his statement, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in explaining iman: 'That you believe in Allah... (2) to its end,' its meaning according to al-Shaykh al-Ash'ari is that you know that, and according to al-Qadi and others is that you speak to yourself with that speech following knowledge (3), and on both sayings, knowledge which is itself iman or necessary for it is not obtained except by correct nazar. And that necessitates that iman on both sayings is not obtained except by correct nazar. And the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, only did not explain their proofs to them because they are rational, not dependent on the Lawgiver's explanation for them, and also because of his sufficiency with what is in the Quran of abundant proofs for them. Rather, he, peace be upon him, explained to them what is not known except from divine law: that knowledge of these characteristics is the legal iman by which entry into Paradise follows even if one does not fulfill the branches of the Law, so that from his interpretation of iman is taken the invalidity of the Mu'tazilite doctrine in making obligatory acts part of it, and that whoever does not fulfill them is not a believer, and also from it is taken their excommunication for their deficiency of one characteristic of the characteristics of iman, which is knowledge of predestination. And among the benefits of his interpretation, peace be upon him, of iman is that the morally responsible person, if he knows its reality, seeks to acquire this reality and know it by correct nazar. But if he does not know the reality of iman, he may acquire knowledge of things extraneous to it, such as the science of stars and medicine and the like, or he may acquire knowledge of some characteristics of iman only, and he deludes, due to his ignorance of the reality of iman, that he has attained its reality and that he is a believer legally, while he is not so. And analogize to these benefits what befits the speech of one who has been given the comprehensive expressions. As for their understanding the validity of taqlid from this hadith, it is not hidden that it is an extremely weak understanding, and what indicates to you the extreme weakness of it, in addition to what preceded, is that taqlid regarding these characteristics by which iman is interpreted is with respect to the establishment of their implications and their correctness.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of an objection. It begins by stating the objection: some people of little insight rely on the famous hadith of Jibril to argue that taqlid (uncritical acceptance) in matters of faith is sufficient. They argue that if nazar (rational inquiry) were necessary, the Prophet would have mentioned proofs when he explained iman. The author then refutes this objection (wa hadha al-akhdhu min al-hadithi batilun qat'an) by explaining the Prophet's silence on proofs: the proofs are rational (aqliyya), not dependent on revelation, and the Qur'an already contains abundant proofs. The Prophet only explained what is known exclusively from revelation—that these characteristics constitute saving faith. The author then draws several benefits: (1) refuting the Mu'tazila who make works part of iman, (2) excommunicating those who deny predestination, and (3) encouraging the seeker to pursue proper nazar. Finally, he stresses that the very idea of using the hadith to justify taqlid is extremely weak, since taqlid is about the truth of the propositions, not about their acceptance without understanding.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Good deeds are part of the definition of iman (Mu'tazilite view).
Correction: Iman is knowledge and assent; works are separate requirements, not part of the essence of iman.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is one benefit of the Prophet's interpretation of iman?
A) It encourages doing good deeds.
B) It refutes the Mu'tazila who make works part of iman.
C) It shows that taqlid is sufficient.
D) It proves that nazar is unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's omission of proofs was deliberate; his explanation provides essential guidance on the reality of iman and its conditions, while firmly rejecting the sufficiency of taqlid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever deluded yourself into thinking you possess the reality of iman while you have only accepted it from others without personal investigation? What is one step you can take today to ensure your faith is based on genuine knowledge?
?
The Prophet defined iman as knowledge of specific characteristics; which of these characteristics do you truly understand and believe in your heart, and which have you merely memorised or assumed? Will you commit to studying and verifying each one seriously?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow and be asked about the reality of iman, would your answer be based on what you have truly sought and understood, or on what you passively inherited? What will you change starting now?

The Logical Impossibility of Taqlid in Belief
Sanusi presents a logical proof against taqlid in foundational beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why taqlid (blind imitation) is logically impossible for foundational beliefs, as Sanusi demonstrates through a circularity argument.

Core Idea
Taqlid in foundational beliefs leads to a logical circle.

Sanusi presents a crisp logical proof that taqlid cannot be the basis for the foundational truths of faith. Even if one were to imitate the highest authority—the Prophet—that imitation would depend on already knowing that he is truly a messenger, which in turn requires knowledge of God and His attributes. This sets up a circular dependency that makes taqlid impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the argument's flow. Note the key terms: taqlid, prophethood, miracle, circularity.
2
Trace the dependency chain
Identify the sequence: taqlid depends on knowing prophethood; prophethood depends on a miracle; a miracle depends on knowing God and His attributes.
The dependency is a chain that loops back on itself.
3
Recognize the circularity
See that if knowledge of God depends on prophethood, and knowledge of prophethood depends on knowing God, we have a circle. This is what Sanusi calls 'al-dawr'.
Circular reasoning is logically invalid.
4
Understand the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that taqlid cannot be the basis for foundational beliefs. Instead, rational proof is necessary.
This is a fundamental principle in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعلى مَنْ يُقلِّدُ في ثبوتها - لو صح التقليد - النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وسائر الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ولا شك أنَّ تقليدهم فيها فرعُ ثبوت رسالتهم ، وهي لا تثبتُ إلا بالمعجزة المتوقفِ معرفةُ دلالتِها على معرفة وجودِهِ تعالى ومعرفة صفاته التي يدخل فيها معرفةً القدر (وإنما دخل القدر في صفاته تعالى؛ لأنه يرجع للعلم والإرادة. « صفاقسي ») فإذاً ؛ لو توقَّفَتْ معرفةُ خصالِ الإيمانِ ـ مِنْ حيثُ ثبوتُها ، لا مِنْ حيثُ إنَّها تفسير للإيمانِ الشرعي - على قول الرسولِ .. لَلزِمَ الدورُ وتوقف الشيء على نفسه .
The highest one to imitate in establishing them — if imitation (taqlid) were valid — is the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, and all the messengers, peace be upon them. There is no doubt that imitating them in these matters is a branch of the establishment of their prophethood, and their prophethood is only established by a miracle (mu'jizah), the knowledge of whose indication depends on knowledge of His existence, may He be exalted, and knowledge of His attributes, which includes knowledge of al-qadar (divine decree). (And qadar is included among His attributes only because it returns to knowledge and will — al-Sfaqsi.) Therefore, if knowledge of the qualities of faith — in terms of their establishment, not in terms of their being an interpretation of legal faith — were dependent on the statement of the Messenger, then circularity (al-dawr) would result, and the thing would depend on itself.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof (burhan) against the validity of taqlid (blind imitation) in matters of belief. Sanusi begins by identifying the highest authority one might imitate—the Prophet and all messengers. Even if taqlid were generally permissible, the problem is that imitating a messenger in these foundational beliefs presupposes that we already know that the messenger is truly a messenger. But establishing prophethood requires a miracle (mu'jizah), and to recognize a miracle as a sign of truthfulness, we must first know that God exists and know His attributes (since a miracle is a divine act). Among those attributes is qadar (divine decree), which relates to God's knowledge and will, as the commentator notes. So we have a circular dependency: to know God we need prophethood, but to know prophethood we need to know God. Therefore, if knowledge of the articles of faith (khisal al-iman) — specifically their being true, not their legal definition — relied solely on the Prophet's statement, it would lead to circular reasoning (al-dawr), meaning a thing depending on itself, which is impossible. Thus, taqlid cannot be the basis for foundational theological knowledge; rational proof is necessary.

Key Terms

ثبوت الرسالة
المعجزة
الدور
صفات الله
القدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think taqlid is acceptable in all religious matters, including foundational beliefs.
Correction: Sanusi shows that taqlid in foundational beliefs leads to logical circularity, making it impossible. Rational proof is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's argument, why would making faith based on taqlid of the Prophet lead to circularity?
A) Because establishing prophethood depends on prior knowledge of God, and knowledge of God depends on prophethood.
B) Because the Prophet forbade taqlid.
C) Because miracles are not reliable.
D) Because faith is a personal matter.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid cannot be the basis for foundational beliefs because it leads to circular reasoning; rational proof must be used.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about God solely because you were taught it, without ever asking yourself if it could be rationally justified? What would it mean for your faith if that belief were based on imitation?
?
If even the Prophet's authority depends on rational proof of God's existence, then where does your own certainty come from? Are you willing to examine the foundations of your faith with the same rigor Sanusi demands?
?
Think of a core belief you hold about Allah. Can you articulate a rational proof for it without appealing to any authority? If not, what step will you take today to move from taqlid to certainty?

Knowledge of Allah is the Best Deed
Hadith on the virtue of knowledge of Allah over action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet (peace be upon him) considered knowledge of Allah superior to action, and how a little action with knowledge outweighs much action without it.

Core Idea
Knowledge of Allah is the foundation that gives all actions their value.

The first proof Sanusi presents is a hadith where the Prophet declares knowledge of Allah as the most virtuous deed. When questioned, he explains that even a small deed done with knowledge of Allah is more beneficial than many deeds done without it. This sets the priority of tawhid over all religious actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the full hadith where the Prophet is asked about the best deed. Notice the surprise of the questioner when the Prophet answers with knowledge instead of action.
The questioner expected a deed like prayer or charity.
2
Understand the Prophet's explanation
Reflect on the Prophet's statement: 'A little action benefits with knowledge of Allah, and much action does not benefit with ignorance of Allah.' Why does knowledge make such a difference?
Knowledge of Allah gives intention and sincerity its correct orientation.
3
Connect to tawhid
Recognize that 'knowledge of Allah' here means knowledge of His essence, attributes, and actions – the core of ilm al-tawhid. This hadith establishes its supreme rank among all sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1 بعضُ الآثارِ والأخبارِ الدالة على شرفِ علم التوحيدِ ] ومما يدلُّ على شرف هذا العلم وعظيم فضلِهِ : ما رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ قيلَ : يا رسولَ اللهِ ؛ أَيُّ الأعمالِ أَفَضلُ ؟ قالَ : « الْعِلْمُ بِاللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ » ، فقيل : يا رسولَ اللهِ ؛ نسألُكَ عنِ العمل ، فتجيب عنِ العلم ؟! فقالَ : « إِنَّ قَلِيلَ الْعَمَلِ يَنْفَعُ مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِاللَّهِ ، وَإِنَّ كَثِيرَ الْعَمَلِ لا يَنْفَعُ مَعَ الْجَهْلِ بِاللهِ (۲) (رواه ابن عبد البر في جامع بيان العلم وفضله) ( ٢١٤ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه ، والقضاعي في « مسند الشهاب » ( ١٠١٥ ) من حديث سیدنا ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه) ورُوِيَ عنه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : أَنَّهُ أتاه رجلٌ فقال له : يا نبي الله ؛ علمْني مِنْ غرائب العلم ، فقال : « مَا فَعَلْتَ فِي رَأْس الْعِلْمِ حَتَّى تَطْلُبَ غَرَائِبَهُ ؟ » ، قال : وما رأسُ العلم يا نبي الله ؟ قالَ : ( أَعَرَفْتَ الرَّبِّ ؟ » ، قال : نعم ، قال : « فَمَا فَعَلْتَ فِي حَفِّهِ عَلَيْكَ ؟ » ، قال : ما شاءَ اللهُ ،  َقالَ : ( أَعَرَفْتَ الْمَوْتَ ؟ » ، قال : نعم ، قال : « فَمَا أَعْدَدْتَ لَهُ ؟ » ، قال : ما شاء الله ، فقال : انْطَلِقْ وَأَحْكِمْ مَا هَا هُنَا ، فَإِذَا أَحْكَمْتَ فَتَعَالَ أُعَلِّمْكَ مِنْ غَرَائِبٍ الْعِلْمِ (۱) (رواه الجوهري في « مسند الموطأ » ( ۱۰ ) ، وابن عبد البر في «جامع بيان العلم وفضله » ( ۱۲۲۲ ) من حديث عبد الله بن المسور رحمه الله تعالى مرسلاً .) ورُوِيَ في الخبرِ : أَنَّ الله تعالى أوحى إلى داود عليه السلام : يا داود ؛ تعلَّم العلم النافع ، قالَ : يَا رَبِّ ، وما العلم النافع ؟ قال : أن تعرف جلالي وعظمتي وكبريائي وكمال قدرتي على كلِّ شيءٍ ، فإِنَّ هذا هو العلم النافع الذي يُقرِّبُكَ إِليَّ (٢) (أورده حجة الإسلام الغزالي في « منهاج العابدين » ( ص ٥١ )، وقد نصح فقال : ( وليكن الطلب طلب دراية ، لا طلب رواية ، واعلم أن الخطر عظيم ، فمن طلب العلم ليصرف به وجوه الناس إليه ، ويجالس به الأمراء ويباهي به النظراء ، ويتصيد به الحكام .. فتجارته بائرة ، وصفقته خاسرة )) وفي القرآن العظيم : إِنَّمَا يَخْشَى اللَّهَ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ الْعُلَمُوا ) (فاطر : ٢٨]
1 Some of the traditions and reports indicating the honor of the science of tawhid: Among what indicates the honor of this science and its great merit is what has been narrated that it was said: O Messenger of God, which deed is most virtuous? He said: ‘Knowledge of God, Almighty and Majestic.’ It was said: O Messenger of God, we ask you about action, and you answer about knowledge?! He said: ‘Indeed, a little action benefits with knowledge of God, and indeed, much action does not benefit with ignorance of God.’ (Reported by Ibn Abd al-Barr in Jami' Bayan al-Ilm wa Fadlihi, 214, from the hadith of our master Anas, may God be pleased with him, and by al-Quda'i in Musnad al-Shihab, 1015, from the hadith of our master Ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him.) And it has been narrated from him, may God bless him and grant him peace, that a man came to him and said: O Prophet of God, teach me from the rare types of knowledge. He said: ‘What have you done with the head of knowledge that you seek its rarities?’ He said: What is the head of knowledge, O Prophet of God? He said: ‘Do you know the Lord?’ He said: Yes. He said: ‘What have you done regarding His right upon you?’ He said: As God wills. He said: ‘Do you know death?’ He said: Yes. He said: ‘What have you prepared for it?’ He said: As God wills. He said: ‘Go and master what is here, and when you have mastered it, then come and I will teach you from the rare types of knowledge.’ (Reported by al-Jawhari in Musnad al-Muwatta, 10, and by Ibn Abd al-Barr in Jami' Bayan al-Ilm wa Fadlihi, 1222, from the hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Musawwar, may God have mercy on him, as a mursal report.) And it has been narrated in the report that God Almighty revealed to David, peace be upon him: O David, learn beneficial knowledge. He said: O Lord, what is beneficial knowledge? He said: That you know My majesty, My greatness, My pride, and the perfection of My power over everything. For this is the beneficial knowledge that brings you near to Me. (Mentioned by the Proof of Islam al-Ghazali in Minhaj al-Abidin, p. 51, and he advised, saying: Let the seeking be seeking of understanding, not seeking of transmission. And know that the danger is great. Whoever seeks knowledge to turn people's faces towards him, to sit with princes, to boast to peers, and to hunt for rulers... his trade is in ruin and his bargain is a loss.)) And in the Mighty Quran: ‘Only those among His servants who are knowledgeable fear God’ [Fatir: 28].
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage collects transmitted proofs (adillah naqliyyah) for the honor and virtue of ilm al-tawhid (knowledge of divine unity). It begins with a subheading indicating that these are some of the traditions (athar) and reports (akhbar) indicating the honor of this science. The first proof is a famous hadith: someone asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about the best deed, and he answered 'knowledge of Allah'. When asked why he answered about knowledge instead of action, he explained that a little action benefits with knowledge of God, but much action does not benefit with ignorance. This establishes the priority of knowledge of God over all actions. The second hadith involves a man asking the Prophet to teach him rare knowledge; the Prophet first asks about the 'head of knowledge' — which is knowing the Lord, and also knowing death and preparing for it. Only after mastering these fundamentals should one seek rare knowledge. This shows that ma'rifat al-Rabb (knowledge of the Lord) is the foundation. The third report is a divine revelation to Prophet David (peace be upon him) about beneficial knowledge: it is knowledge of God's majesty, greatness, pride, and perfect power. This knowledge draws one closer to God. A note from al-Ghazali warns against seeking such knowledge for worldly purposes. Finally, the Quranic verse (Fatir: 28) states that only the knowledgeable (al-'ulama) truly fear God, linking knowledge of Him with reverential fear (khashyah). Together, these texts argue for the supreme value and necessity of learning tawhid.

Key Terms
العلم بالله
معرفة الله
فضل العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that outward deeds like prayer and charity are more important than knowledge.
Correction: This hadith shows that knowledge of Allah is the root; deeds branch from it. Without knowledge, deeds lose their value.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this lesson, why does a little action benefit with knowledge of Allah?
A) Because knowledge itself is a deed
B) Because knowledge ensures deeds are done with sincerity and correctness
C) Because deeds are not required if one has knowledge
D) Because the Prophet preferred knowledge over action

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of Allah is the most virtuous pursuit because it gives all other actions their worth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you first ensure it is built on knowledge of Allah? If not, what is one thing you will learn about Allah this week to transform your next action?
?
Think of a small deed you did today—did it arise from a conscious connection to Allah, or was it routine? How would the deed feel different if you had just studied a name of Allah before doing it?
?
The Prophet said that much action without knowledge of Allah is useless. Is there an area in your life where you are 'doing a lot' but have not sought knowledge of Allah about it? What step will you take today to replace ignorance with knowledge?
